The pork roll was amazing, very nice fat content and great chew and sauce. The potato salad was on point with the cucumber slices. Also their tartar sauce was amazing, it's more sauce than paste like most places.</Text>

I inquired about adopting a 8 month old shepherd and filled out an application online.  I owned a shepherd for 13 years and he passed away in July.  I am a homeowner with a full time job and my house has a 1/2 acre fenced yard.

I was shocked when the representative called me and said my application was denied! She said it was denied because on the application I said the dog would be outside (in the huge yard) during the day and inside the house at night.  I answered this way because the dog will not be confined in a small house all day.  I put on the application my girlfriend would be home during the day with the dog.  I tried to explain to the rep my girlfriend would let the dog in and out of the house as he pleases but she wasn‚Äôt hearing it.  She lectured me about how a dog is supposed to be part of the family and inside all day like her dogs.  She finished by telling me I would never be able to adopt from them and she recommended I check a municipal shelter or buy one from a breeder.  What a joke.  I try to adopt a dog and give him a amazing life ( like I gave my previous shepherd for 13 years) and she tells me to go to a breeder yet they advertise they need more donations and willing people to adopt.  Unbelievable<//review>

< Text>
I adopted a puppy from GSROC last summer, and I can't say enough good things about the organization, the adoption experience, and my baby. First, this organization is such an asset to the region. They save so many German Shepherds and other dogs who would otherwise die in public shelters. Second, from start to finish, the adoption process was professional and smooth. GSROC has wonderful volunteers who are available, helpful, and diligent. Third, and definitely saving the best for last, my puppy is the AMAZING. He is a big beautiful purebred who is calm, smart, and everything a GSD should be. I give GSROC an A+!< /Text>

< review>
I love everything about this restaurant. It's in a great neighborhood, the food is incredible, and the atmosphere is... well, it's unusual. Unless you come with a party of 6 be prepared to share a table with strangers. There really isn't much space between tables, so occasionally you'll be aware of the people at the table next to you, as well. That's the closest to a negative that I can come up with, and the food more than makes up for whatever discomfort that might cause.< /review>

< Review>
This rescue is not really looking to find the right dog for you. They just want the money for a dog they picked up from a shelter for free. If you don't want to be pressured, this is not the place for you. We met 3 dogs, fostered one for them and even donated supplies for them.

When we didn't like the fact they had another potential family waiting to see a dog after us and we weren't comfortable making a decision with that type of pressure, they said we were too difficult to make a match with and now refuse to respond to us. They won't even give us a receipt for the more than $100 of dog food, collar, toys and other stuff we donated.

They just want to make quick flips with dogs they "rescued" from shelters. Felt like a used car deal and there was no recourse if you got a lemon. They like having their hands out for money and donations,, but when it comes to truly helping a family that has a toddler find the right dog they just dismiss you completely.

There are much better options for finding your next family member. Go somehwere else!<//Review>

<Text>I would like to respond to the review posted by Rachel Weaver.
As an active volunteer, I can personally guarantee that what this person has written in her first two sentences could not be any further from the truth. GSROC pays to spay or neutered every dog that comes into the rescue ; pays to board the dogs at a private boarding facility, and pays for good quality food & supplements while the dog is in their care.  These are the expenses for a healthy dog. Now, when they bring in a sick dog (which is done regularly) GSROC also pays all the vet bills to get the dog healthy before the dog is placed. Typically, GSROC pays a significantly higher amount of $$ to take care of the dog,  then what is asked for as an adoption donation. To suggest GSROC is ‚Äúflipping dogs for financial gain‚Äù is completely ludicrous. And reflects an uninformed individual.

This particular family needed a GSD with very specific characteristics. They needed a dog to be good with a toddler and a smaller dog. Plus they wanted a specific size and color. Over the course of several months, the rescue carefully selected, talked to the family, showed pictures, discussed temperament, and upon the families agreement, showed this family at least 5 dogs/puppies that were a match. However, with each pup, they declined the dog for one reason or another. Including a beautiful, calm, friendly female that bonded with the child and husband almost immediately. They passed on her because of her COLOR. Weeks later, The family came to an adoption event where they ‚Äúfell in love‚Äù with a dog. GSROC  needed to have them bring their dog to the kennel for a meet & greet to evaluate compatibility. They did that the following day and volunteers observed the dogs were completely compatible. However, the family would not commit to adopt the dog but wanted to foster her instead. At that time, there was another family waiting to meet this dog. Since the Weaver family was not willing to adopt the dog, the rescue moved on to showing that dog to the other family, who adopted her.< /Text><Rating>4</Rating></record>

<Date>1598132943237</Date><rate>5</rate>< Review>
Thanks to GSROC, I am a first time dog owner! I had a phenomenal experience working with them in finding a great fit for myself and also the dog. GSROC takes good care of their dogs and provides all the resources needed (such as additional training) to ensure that their dogs are friendly and well behaved.

After completing a very thorough application, Maria from GSROC reached out to me and suggested that I meet with JJ since he was a calm German Shepherd and would be great for a first timer like me. During the meeting, I quickly found that he was too big for myself and my girlfriend. We weren‚Äôt sure we‚Äôd be able to handle this big boy, so Maria brought out another dog. Much to our surprise, she brought out a 2 year old husky pup - Juneau! He was a perfect size for us and we quickly agreed to foster him. We were given everything we needed to take care of him.

After we took him home, Maria arranged private training sessions for us so that Juneau‚Äôs stubborn behavior could improve. After a month, there‚Äôs a huge difference in his self-control and obedience. Juneau became irresistible to us and we decided to adopt him. Gabi with GSROC helped answer my many questions regarding the adoption process.

GSROC provided great care in terms of helping us select the right dog and the training needed to turn this stubborn foster into our lovable dog.<//Review>

<Rate>5<//Rate><Review>Everyone is a volunteer.  They work to help/provide for any German Shepherd Dog in need and placement as well. They do "fostering home" for the dogs.
Been involved with them for about 20+ years, donating.
I recommend them highly.
Remember, the German Shepherd puppy looks cute when small.
When they grow, they get bigger and demand more physically active attention and TRAINING/OBEDIENCE.
Need a sizeable yard for them to play etc. At least an hour a day plus at least 1 mile trot/walk.
Apt's/condo's dont cut it.
These ARE working dogs.
If you dont work them they can get frustrated and become destructive. You dont walk away and forget them.
Not every home is meant to have a GSD.
Think, before you add a GSD to your pack. Can you do this for at least 10+ years, without delay?
NEVER abandon a GSD, EVER!
Love/respect them, they will love/respect you.
Expect a follower, closer than a shadow.  You wont regret it, EVER!<//Review>< Name>
dave cruzen</Name>

< text>
The GSROC are a great organization.  They truly care about the dogs and the adopters.  They want to make sure the dogs are a fit for their future owners and vice versa.  I had very specific needs in my home and all the dogs I viewed online that I wanted would not be a fit.  Steve the adoption coordinator had a couple of dogs that would fit my particular needs and I came to visit them at the rescue.  It is a great place to meet your potential furry family member.  The first few days of my adoption of Peter aka Buddy was not a very smooth transition.  I contacted Steve at GSROC with some major concerns and he put me in touch with their in house professional trainer.  They both wanted to make sure that Buddy was the right dog for my family.  It has been about a month now and I could not ask for a better dog.  He is exactly the fit I needed for my family.  I am glad that I chose GSROC and not another rescue.  If you are looking for a new furry family member and are not sure of which rescue to choose, I definitely recommend German Shepherd Rescue of Orange County.</text>

< review>
Share review

Embed review

Write an update

Edit review

12/27/2019
I stopped in this store to exchange a skateboard that I had purchased at the Redding store. Redding store sold me this board even though it looked as though it may have been used before. The deck looked a little scuffed but I did not mind until I realized one of the bearings were defective. I called the Chico store manager (Xavier) and explained the situation in great detail and he said to bring it in for an exchange.

I drove from Stirling City to Zumiez in Chico only to have Xavier try to tell me the board had been used and he could not do the exchange. I explained to him that the Redding store manager sold me this board exactly as it is. He had a hard time believing that the Redding store Manager would sell a board in this condition and made it very clear by sub-texting and condescending tones that he did not believe me. After once again explaining to him what I already discussed over the phone, he decided to do the exchange.

This is where he became rude and unfriendly, ESPECIALLY being the fact that he's the leader of this store. While my daughter was choosing another board I couldn't stop overhearing him continue to subtext to employees about the condition of the board and how he just could not believe Redding store manager would sell me a board in this condition. I grew irritated and confronted Xavier by saying, "I feel disrespected because I'm being called a liar". That statement must have offended him because he threatened to have me exchange it at another Zumiez store. This would have required me to drive at least another hour to another Zumiez store. I explained to him that he's the one being offensive with his subtle accusations and sub-texting.

During the exchange he realized that I was telling the truth when he saw the employee's name on my receipt and the 10% "markdown" the GM from Redding store applied. Before this he was ADAMANT on how no one from the Redding store, especially the GM Javier (who held a higher position than him), would never sell me a board in this condition. At this point he literally appeared dazed and confused. I finally asked if the exchange was complete so I could leave the store. He said yes and he still seemed to be in awe over the situation. On my way out I made it clear to him (for the 10th time) that I'm an honest person with integrity.

After all that this Store Manager Xavier didn't even offer me an apology. I will never come back to any Zumiez store. This Xavier fellow is a very rude, condescending, and frail man.< /review>

<Review>It's pretty decent. What I like most is the friendly, helpful staff & most of their stuff is priced pretty fair- clothes mainly. And I've bought several clothing items from this place so I'd know lol their garments last WAY longer than similar items I've bought at Walmart. Yeah, I'm a budget shopper, how could u tell lol

Oh and another strong point I feel merits mentioning in its own paragraph: the great hours! Being open until 11pm in this remote location is so amazing bcuz many times I've needed something like cough meds for the kids or ginger ale, soup, ice etc. in a pinch and it's either too late for a drive in town or just don't feel the drive. I love it.

< text>
Ok to be fair, this is of course a fast food restaurant. However, in all the fast food restaurants, this one is really our favorite!

Often we are so tired from work and just looking to have a quick dinner. Noodles & Company is always reliable, and with the free delivery from DoorDash it‚Äôs just the place for that last minute delicious lifesaver.

For those who‚Äôve never been there, Noodles & Company has a very simple menu. Few noodle choices served with different sauces like pesto, Alfredo, marinara... But the thing that appealing is that all their menu items can be made vegetarian! All of them!

I would highly recommend you‚Äôre try the Pesto Caviapatti. And the spaghetti Alfredo is one my favorites. Also FYI: their Mac-and-cheese side and tomato bisque soups are fantastic! Totally worth the extra $3.</text>

< text>
COVID MITIGATION REVIEW

PB Vet has been my veterinary clinic for 4 years now and they are so friendly and helpful. They treat your animals like an extension of their own family and its clear how passionate they are for their work.
I only give 4 stars because of how absolutely long it takes for them to see your pet. As with many vets, they have started coming outside to retrieve your pet from you. I have waited outside with my dogs for upwards of 45 minutes past my scheduled appointment, and that's on average. < review>
Southern California University of Health Sciences is a sham and the employees there are bullies! Don't waste your time, and more importantly your money applying or attending.

I applied to both their DC and PA programs and was first accepted into their DC program. After my acceptance, I kept receiving admissions emails regarding my "admission to their PA program." When I called the school to report the irregularity, I was told by Ms Elizabeth Cruz the email had been sent in error. Strangely, Ms Elizabeth Cruz also told me at that time that applicants were expected to be "professional throughout the application process." - Apparently Ms Elizabeth Cruz says this to "everyone" (despite never saying this to me at any time during our previous phone calls before that).

It wasn't after I called to follow up on my PA application (months later) that I was told (more so screamed at) by Mr David Coronado, who told me I would not be accepted into their PA program and that my DC acceptance had been rescinded because I had "altered" their admission emails... When I tried to ask where this accusation was coming from, Mr David Coronado refused to let me speak and threatened to report me to CASPA. When I tried to justify the validity of the emails I had received, Mr Coronado raised his voice at me and told me that my opinion did not matter.

Well after months of being told I'd get a call back from the dean of the DC and PA program (which never occurred), I was able to settle the situation with the school and obtain an apology. The school did in fact report me to CASPA and I was also able to obtain a retraction for their libelous claim. At this point I have no desire to attend this school and was glad to see the reality about SCUHS before becoming part of the student body.

Ultimately SCUHS and its staff lack the professionalism required to operate a health sciences school and SCUHS' action only discredits the legitimacy of the school. While SCHUS is tasked with training our future healthcare providers, the school doesn't seem to know what it is doing at the administrative level...</review>

< Review>
I have been a very loyal customer for almost 8 years.  I have sent these reviews with always a max rating.
But today it's different.  I have been asking for Nat'l to have their drivers that return cars to the lot lower the seats because I always hit my head when entering the car. And to this day! Nothing has ever been done.
Also the car was washed, but still wet over all the windows plus inside windows were dirty.  There was mud on the floor door jam that should have been cleaned prior to delivering the car.
This is not an isolated incident!  I travel the Western US and only use Nat'l. This seems to be at most of the rental yards. Cars not cleaned, Seats not lowered and the biggest pet peeve is the tank is not full when i select a car.  This has only happened twice in 7.5 years.

< Review>
I will start off saying my flight was delayed about 1 hour. However, I don't think that that was a big impact on my experience.

When I arrived, there were no vehicles available. There were about 10-15 people waiting to get a vehicle. As vehicles were brought out, the person at the front of the line was offered that one, and if declined, it was offered to the next. So, there was a very limited choice. It took me about 30 mins before I got an SUV or minivan (after turning down a small car that would not have held my luggage and an extra person or two).

When checking out, I asked about the line, and was told it had been that way since mid morning (I got there about 2:00pm), thus, I don't think it was my flight delay that caused this problem.

This seems to be a common problem across multiple National Car rentals at airports.< /Review>
